How to Clean Up Your Messy Windows Context Men= u

Walter Glenn @wjglenn
Updated Jul 5, 2017, 6:34 pm EST | 10 min read

If you=E2=80=99ve ever found yourself right-clicking on something and wo= ndering where all that junk came from, you=E2=80=99re not alone. Want to ge= t rid of the cruft you don=E2=80=99t use, and add some actually useful item= s to the context menu? You can.

Windows includes a bunch of options in that context menu by default, and= that list grows as you install more apps. It sometimes seems like every ap= p is fighting for a piece of your context menu and most of us don=E2=80=99t= even use half of them. We=E2=80=99re going to show you how you can re= move items by editing your Registry, as well as an easier cleanup method us= ing a couple of free third-party apps. We=E2=80=99ll also point you toward = how to add some more useful commands. Without too much effort, you can= take your context menu from being cluttered and only mostly useful=E2= =80=A6

=E2=80=A6to being streamlined and efficient.

Let=E2=80=99s get started.

The Hard Way: Remove Items from the C= ontext Menu by Editing the Registry

If you want to clean things up the truly geeky way, you can do from Regi= stry Editor without the need for third-party software. We=E2=80=99ll get to= the easier tools a bit later, but we think it helps when using those tools= to understand how this stuff is handled in the Registry.

Standard warning: Registry Editor is a powerful tool an= d misusing it can render your system unstable or even inoperable. If you=E2= =80=99ve never worked with it before, consider reading about how to use the Registry Editor before you get started. And definitely=  back up the Registry (and you= r computer!) before making changes. This is especially true when follow= ing the guidelines in this article, because you=E2=80=99ll end up having to= do a little hunting around to find the context menu entries that mean some= thing to you.

RELATED: Learning to Use th= e Registry Editor Like a Pro

Open the Registry Editor by hitting Start and typing =E2=80=9Cregedit.= =E2=80=9D Press Enter to open Registry Editor and then give it permiss= ion to make changes to your PC.

Unfortunately, the items populating your context menu are not all locate= d in the same place in the Registry. You can find most of the context menu = items used for both files and folders by drilling down to one of the follow= ing keys in the navigation pane on the left:

HKEY_CLASSES_ROOT\*\shell
HKEY_CLASSES_ROOT\*\shellex\ContextMenuHandlers
HKEY_CLASSES_ROOT\AllFileSystemObjects\ShellEx

You=E2=80=99ll find context menu items specific to just folders in one o= f these keys instead:

HKEY_CLASSES_ROOT\Directory\shell
HKEY_CLASSES_ROOT\Directory\shellex\ContextMenuHandlers

RELATED: How to Bookma= rk Locations in the Windows Registry

You=E2=80=99ll need to handle the context menu items found in these loca= tions a bit differently, so keep reading and we=E2=80=99ll explain how. For= now, you might find it handy to locate each of those locations in the= Registry and add them to your favorites list so t= hat they=E2=80=99re easier to browse through later.

Remove =E2=80=9CShell=E2=80=9D Items

Let=E2=80=99s take a look at one item as an example. I use the VLC video playe= r. When I installed it, VLC added a context menu item named =E2=80=9CAdd to= VLC media player=E2=80=99s Playlist.=E2=80=9D I never use that and would r= ather it not be on my context menu.

Here=E2=80=99s how we get rid of that menu item. In Registry Editor= , drill down to the following key:

HKEY_CLASSES_ROOT\Directory\shell\AddtoPlaylistVLC

I spotted the AddtoPlaylistVLC key while browsing through t= he shell key looking for items to remove. Items under the regu= lar shell key are usually really easy to spot and deal with.

We have a few options on how to handle this. We could just delete that <= code>AddToPlaylistVLC key entirely, and that would remove the item f= rom the context menu. However, unless you back up your Registry=E2=80=94or = export the key first and keep up with the REG file=E2=80=94it won=E2=80=99t= be easy to get back if you change your mind.

The second option is to disable the key instead of deleting it. To do th= at, just right-click the AddToPlaylistVLC key=E2=80=94or whate= ver key you=E2=80=99re working with=E2=80=94and choose New > String Valu= e. Name the new string value =E2=80=9CLegacyDisable.=E2=80=9D

As soon as you create the LegacyDisable value, the change s= hould be immediate. Right-click a file or folder in File Explorer and we ca= n see that the =E2=80=9CAdd to VLC media player=E2=80=99s Playlist=E2= =80=9D item has been removed from the context menu.

You also have a third option. If you occasionally use a menu item, but d= on=E2=80=99t want it cluttering up your regular context menu, you can hide = it away on the extended context menu you see only when you hold Shift while= right-clicking a file or folder. To do this, right-click the AddToPl= aylistVLC key=E2=80=94or whatever key you=E2=80=99re working with=E2= =80=94and choose New > String Value. Name the new string value =E2=80=9C= Extended.=E2=80=9D

Now, it will only appear if you right-click on a folder while holding Sh= ift.

Remove =E2=80=9CShellex=E2=80=9D Items

You probably noticed that some of the common Registry keys we listed at = the top of this section have =E2=80=9Cshellex=E2=80=9D (Shell Extension) in= the name instead of just =E2=80=9Cshell=E2=80=9D. You=E2=80=99ll need to h= andle those types of keys just a bit differently. As our example, we=E2=80= =99ll head down to one of those keys we mentioned:

HKEY_CLASSES_ROOT\Directory\shellex\ContextMenuHandlers

The shellex items will be a little tougher to decipher, but you can usua= lly figure out an item by the key name on the left. Here, we=E2=80=99re goi= ng to be working with the DropboxExt key inside the ContextMenuHandlers key.

When Dropbox is installed, it adds a =E2=80=9CMove to Dropbox=E2=80=9D c= ommand to the context menu. Because I=E2=80=99m more of a drag and dro= pper, I=E2=80=99ve never once used that command, and I=E2=80=99m going to g= et rid of it.

You can=E2=80=99t use the tricks with the LegacyDisable and Extended string values we described above with shellex i= tems. You could still delete the whole DropboxExt key to remov= e it from the context menu (and be sure to back the key up if you do), but = there is a simple way to disable it. Just select the key on the left a= nd then double-click the (Default) value inside that key to open its proper= ties window.

On the properties window, in the =E2=80=9CValue data=E2=80=9D box, just = modify the value that=E2=80=99s already there by putting a few dashes in fr= ont of it, being careful not to delete any of the existing value. That way,= if you change your mind, you can just go back in and remove the dashes. Wh= en you=E2=80=99re done, click =E2=80=9COK.=E2=80=9D

The change will be immediate, so go right-click something in File Explor= er and make sure the command is gone.

Unfortunately, when it comes to shellex items, there=E2=80=99s no way to= hide them on the Extended context menu the way you can with shell items. Y= ou can only delete or disable them.

Explore Other Locations by File Type

If you want to remove context menu items that you only see when you righ= t-click specific types of files, you can do that, too. These items are stor= ed elswhere than the common locations we=E2=80=99ve already looked at. To f= ind them, you=E2=80=99ll need to first locate the file extension key b= y looking under HKEY_CLASSES_ROOT for that extension, which in= turn will tell you the name of the key that you need to look for.

Just as an example, say you wanted to remove the menu item for opening a= n Excel document (XLSX) in Excel when you right-click on it. Why would you = want to do this? Well, you probably wouldn=E2=80=99t, but it=E2=80=99s an e= asy example to look at here. Other applications may add different types of = commands you don=E2=80=99t need.

You=E2=80=99d start by taking a look at the following Registry key for t= he XLSX extension:

HKEY_CLASSES_ROOT\.xlsx

The data column for the (Default) shell key lets you know t= hat the actual type of file is =E2=80=9CExcel.Sheet.12.=E2=80=9D

Now, you can browse to that extensions key:

HKEY_CLASSES_ROOT\Excel.Sheet.12\shell

And now that you=E2=80=99ve located the correct shell key, = you can use the same techniques we described in the previous section on =E2= =80=9Cshell=E2=80=9D items to delete, disable, or hide the item on the Exte= nded context menu. Remember the LegacyDisable and Extend= ed string values? Yep, those work here, too.

The Easy Way: Remove Items from the C= ontext Menu with NirSoft Utilities

So, now that you know how to do things the hard way, let=E2=80=99s take = a look at the easy way. Instead of editing the Registry, you can download t= wo tools from NirSoft to clean up your context menu. Why two tools? Because= one of them handles regular shell items and one handles shellex items. The= y are both much easier to use than editing the Registry, but the behin= d-the-scenes understanding of how these things are handled in the Registry = will give you a leg up in sorting through all the items these tools display= .

RELATED: <= em>How Do I Know if I=E2=80=99m Running 32-bit or 64-bit Windows?

Start by downloading both the tools. The first tool is ShellMenuView, which handl= es regular shell items. The second tool is ShellExView, which handles shellex items. Scroll= down toward the bottom of both those pages to find the download links. The= tools both work with pretty much any version of Windows from 98 all the wa= y through 10. You will need to grab either the 32-bit or 64-bit version, de= pending on whether you=E2=80=99re runn= ing a 32-bit or 64-bit edition of Windows.

The first tool we=E2=80=99ll check out is ShellMenuView, which allows us= to manage all of those regular shell items with an easy to use interface. = After downloading and extracting the tool, double-click the EXE file to run= it. It=E2=80=99s a portable tool, so there=E2=80=99s no installation.

In the ShellMenuView window, just browse down the list until you find th= e item you want to disable. You can only disable items with these tools=E2= =80=94not delete them or hide them on the Extended context menu. And by the= way, these tools disable items by creating a LegacyDisable&nb= sp;string value inside the appropriate key=E2=80=94just like we did when we= edited the Registry manually.

When you find the item you=E2=80=99re looking for, click the =E2=80=9CDi= sable=E2=80=9D button on the toolbar (the red light).

Another benefit of using these tools is that you can select multiple ite= ms and then disable them all at once. In our example, we=E2=80=99re disabli= ng the =E2=80=9CAdd to VLC media player=E2=80=99s Playlist=E2=80=9D item on= ly when you right-click a folder (the same example we used in the Registry = section previously), but we could easily select all of the =E2=80=9CAdd to = VLC media player=E2=80=99s Playlist=E2=80=9D items and then click =E2=80=9C= Disable=E2=80=9D to remove that command from the context menu of all suppor= ted file types as well.

When you=E2=80=99re done removing shell items, the next step is to fire = up the ShellExView tool and remove shellex items. This one works the e= xactly the same way as the first tool. Just select one or more items and th= en click the =E2=80=9CDisable=E2=80=9D button to remove the items from your= context menu.

How to Remove Additional Items from t= he Context Menu

There are a couple of context menu items you may have noticed that neith= er the NirSoft tools nor the regular Registry methods we covered address: n= amely, the items you find on the =E2=80=9COpen With=E2=80=9D and =E2=80=9CS= end To=E2=80=9D submenus.

RELATED: How to Rem= ove Programs from the "Open With" Context Menu in Windows=

The =E2=80=9COpen With=E2=80=9D menu is a handy feature when you op= en files with multiple programs. Whenever you open a file with a particular= program, that program gets added to the =E2=80=9COpen With=E2=80=9D menu f= or that type of file. If you=E2=80=99ve ever accidentally opened a file wit= h the wrong program or with a program you don=E2=80=99t use any more, thoug= h, you=E2=80=99ve probably seen that menu get cluttered over time. Fortunat= ely, we have a complete set of instructions to guide you through removing programs from the =E2=80=9COpen With=E2=80=9D menu.

The =E2=80=9CSend To=E2=80=9D menu is one of those features that people = tend to either love and use all the time or just never even bother with. Wh= en you install Windows, some items are added to the =E2=80=9CSend To=E2=80= =9D menu by default. Others get added over time as you install different ap= ps. If you=E2=80=99ve ever wished you could declutter that menu, it=E2=80= =99s your lucky day! We=E2=80=99ve got one guide for customizing the items on the =E2=80=9CSend To=E2=80=9D menu and anot= her guide if you=E2=80=99d like to remove the =E2=80=9CSend To=E2=80=9D menu from your context menu altogether.

RELATED: Customize= the Send To Menu in Windows 10, 8, 7, or Vista

How to Add Some Useful Items to the C= ontext Menu

Now that you=E2=80=99ve spent some time removing items you don=E2=80=99t= need from your context menu, you can turn your attention to adding some it= ems you might actually use. To start with, you can actually add just about = any application or shortcut you want to the context menu= . Since you=E2=80=99ve now read all about what Registry keys to look throug= h when you=E2=80=99re removing stuff, you won=E2=80=99t be suprised that ad= ding things involves a lot of those same keys.

RELATED: <= strong>How to Add Any Application to the Windows Desktop Right-Click Me= nu

Of course, we wouldn=E2=80=99t leave you without any specific suggestion= s for fun things to add to your context menu. And we=E2=80=99ve covered a b= unch of them. For example, you could add any of the following to your menu:=

  • An =E2=80=9COpen with Notepad= =E2=80=9D command for all files
  • An =E2=80=9COpen PowerShell Here=E2= =80=9D command for folders
  • A =E2=80=9CDefragment=E2=80=9D comma= nd for drives
  • A =E2=80=9CTake Ownership=E2= =80=9D command for files and folders
  • A = command for copying the list of files in a folder
  • A =E2=80=9CControl Panel=E2=80=9D com= mand for quick access

So, have fun and get creative!

We admit, it=E2=80=99s a good amount of information to absorb just to ch= ange a menu that you=E2=80=99ve probably grown used to, but you might be su= rprised at how much more pleasant it is using a nice, clean context menu th= at has commands you=E2=80=99ll actually use. So what are you waiting for? T= ime to get started making those context menus more useful!
